<div id="review_2556506603" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2556506603" />
    <a title="Stephanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21495558-stephanie"><img alt="Stephanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499885866p2/21495558.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2556506603?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie" href="/user/show/21495558-stephanie">Stephanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21495558-stephanie?shelf=ya-realistic-fiction">ya-realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2556506603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10104478493991897377">I absolutely loved this book. And not just because it's all about a high school track star (confession: I ran varsity track and cross country all through high school so all the nerdy running stuff? Yeah, I get it).<br/><br/>First of all, it's <i>clean</i>. No profanity, no sex, no drinking and/or drug use. None of the content that makes contemporary YA edgy these days. And it's a breath of fresh air because you know what? I didn't miss any of that stuff one bit.<br/><br/>That's not to say Van Draanen shied away from deali</span>
  <span id="freeText10104478493991897377" style="display:none">I absolutely loved this book. And not just because it's all about a high school track star (confession: I ran varsity track and cross country all through high school so all the nerdy running stuff? Yeah, I get it).<br /><br />First of all, it's <i>clean</i>. No profanity, no sex, no drinking and/or drug use. None of the content that makes contemporary YA edgy these days. And it's a breath of fresh air because you know what? I didn't miss any of that stuff one bit.<br /><br />That's not to say Van Draanen shied away from dealing with difficult subjects because she didn't. Jessica's struggle to adapt to life without a limb/with a prosthesis felt very real as did the difficulties her parents' faced trying to pay her hospital bills. And I love the way Van Draanen uses Jessica's growing friendship with Rosa to show that everyone deserves to be seen, no matter their abilities.<br /><br />What I loved about this book more than anything, is how hopeful it made me feel. The characters in this book did nice things for others because they genuinely cared for them. And you know what? I love that. We live in a society where it seems like no one has anything nice to say about anyone anymore. The criticism and the negativity that is so rampant on social media today is overwhelming. But this book? This book is inspiring. Even when things are at their worst, it's still easy to root for Jessica because she is a genuinely likeable character. Of course, there's conflict. Of course, there are a few unpleasant characters. But Van Draanen doesn't let negativity dominate the story, and for that I'm thankful.<br /><br />If we, as a society, need the harsh, gritty stories to keep us grounded, we need stories like <i>The Running Dream</i> even more because they give us hope. And hope, ladies and gentlemen, is what gets us out of bed in the morning.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10104478493991897377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4093705594874605674" style="display:none">5 glorious stars to this one! What a wonderful and brave story! <br /><br />I often find myself steering clear of falling and getting back stories these days. Often they feel manipulative and contrived. But The Running Dream, now this is a genuinely good story about falling and getting back up. The tone is honest and sincere. Wendelin Van Draanen made every character in The Running Dream relatable/understandable. Jessica's story is about losing and winning. The Running Dream is more about the love of life than just a book about running. Jessica's pain and Jessica's jubilation, you want to be there for her. You want to chant Run Strong and cheer her over the finish line. Apart from the main theme of loss of carrying on, it was also about how people perceive the differently abled, even though we are all, at our core, so similar. <br /><br />The Running Dream is an eye opener and one that makes you laugh and cry. This was a genuinely heartwarming tale. I loved every bit of it!</span>

<div id="review_1122112940" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1122112940" />
    <a title="alisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34549316-alisha"><img alt="alisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418175711p2/34549316.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1122112940?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="alisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="alisha" href="/user/show/34549316-alisha">alisha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375866289" href="/book/show/12705331-the-running-dream">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1122112940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer48027986448476703">I’m a very unathletic person. I don’t tend to enjoy exercising and don’t play sports, so for me to say that The Running Dream by Wendelin Van Draanen made me want to get up and run is high praise in itself. <br/><br/>The Running Dream follows 16 year old Jessica through her journey of grief and healing as she attempts to live life as an amputee. Her loss of her leg means the possibility of running (Jessica’s main passion) seems to be just a dream - unattainable. <br/><br/>One of the reasons I rated this book highly</span>
  <span id="freeText48027986448476703" style="display:none">I’m a very unathletic person. I don’t tend to enjoy exercising and don’t play sports, so for me to say that The Running Dream by Wendelin Van Draanen made me want to get up and run is high praise in itself. <br /><br />The Running Dream follows 16 year old Jessica through her journey of grief and healing as she attempts to live life as an amputee. Her loss of her leg means the possibility of running (Jessica’s main passion) seems to be just a dream - unattainable. <br /><br />One of the reasons I rated this book highly is because Draanen manages to convey a feeling of real grief. Jessica is a relatable character in the sense that her feelings feel real. She’s not optimistic at first, and it takes time for her to heal. Also, it’s obvious that Draanen thoroughly explored the process of getting new prosthetics and living as an amputee. Draanen did not simplify living as an amputee, or over look the facts that often are skipped over because they’re more gory or harder to deal with. Overall, Draanen’s use of realism made the book touching, it made it feel like you were in Jessica’s story, and in her world. <br /><br />Draanen also touches on topics that that don’t just apply to amputees or those with disabilities - but everyone. One of the quotes from the book that made me see things in a new light was, “I wonder about the deep, wide abyss between good intentions and concrete action, and how many of [the people of her town] lept over it.” The quote is very applicable and inspired me to want to do something. It reminded me that the way to make change happen is to act, something that we don’t often do even though we’re sympathetic to a cause. Also the quote represents a main theme in the book - which is that evolution of the mind and body occur through action, determination, and hard work. <br /><br />The Running Dream also delved into the idea of “seeing [a person], not their disability”. Because of this, the book reminded me of Out of My Mind by Sharon Draper. Out of My Mind is about a girl with cerebral palsy, similar to Rosa, a character who has cerebral palsy in The Running Dream. Both explored the territory of teen characters living with disabilities and their journeys, and both share the similar theme of looking past ones disability and seeing them as a person.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to anyone and everyone, runner or not. The Running Dream is one of those books you zoom through and never forget. Jessica’s story is a true inspiration, it reminds us of everything we have that we forget to be thankful for and take for granted, but more importantly how to keep pushing through the challenges we face. </span>
  <a data-text-id="48027986448476703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer784318890" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15158880382286143568">This book was outstanding! It will definitely stick with me for the rest of my life. It made me appreciate my life and what/who I have. After reading this book I've definitely changed my way on how I see people with disabilities- not that I ever saw disabled people in a bad way- but it's made me realize that there's way more to them then there condition and that I should take the time to get to know them. Also, since I enjoy exercise and running it also motivated me a whole lot more to just get </span>
  <span id="freeText15158880382286143568" style="display:none">This book was outstanding! It will definitely stick with me for the rest of my life. It made me appreciate my life and what/who I have. After reading this book I've definitely changed my way on how I see people with disabilities- not that I ever saw disabled people in a bad way- but it's made me realize that there's way more to them then there condition and that I should take the time to get to know them. Also, since I enjoy exercise and running it also motivated me a whole lot more to just get out as much as possible because you never know when your ability to walk or run or whatever can be taken away. Never take what you have for granted because it can be taken away from you in an instant. I loved everything about this book, whether it was the fact it made me realize all those things above ^ or whether it was the friendships, family support/struggles that happened in this book. Almost every character was so loving and supportive towards Jessica through her journey of learning to live with one leg, never being able to run again (Or so she thought) or just anything else that came her way. It was so inspiring to read this book and I highly suggest that you pick it up and read it now if you haven't already! This deserves way more then 5/5. Just, wow.</span>

    <a title="Joyce Yattoni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15743014-joyce-yattoni"><img alt="Joyce Yattoni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405555367p2/15743014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1075692948?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joyce Yattoni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joyce Yattoni" href="/user/show/15743014-joyce-yattoni">Joyce Yattoni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1075692948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer681737428069337748">This book has been out for awhile, 2012 to be exact and has been on my TBR pile too long. It was the pick me up I needed this week. The audio was superb and gave me some flexibility during a hectic schedule. Talk about restoring my faith in humanity. Jessica, a junior in high school, was involved in a school bus accident. She could have felt sorry for herself when she lost her leg, but showed great determination, grit and humility as she fought for a "normal" life. I loved, loved, loved Fiona, h</span>
  <span id="freeText681737428069337748" style="display:none">This book has been out for awhile, 2012 to be exact and has been on my TBR pile too long. It was the pick me up I needed this week. The audio was superb and gave me some flexibility during a hectic schedule. Talk about restoring my faith in humanity. Jessica, a junior in high school, was involved in a school bus accident. She could have felt sorry for herself when she lost her leg, but showed great determination, grit and humility as she fought for a "normal" life. I loved, loved, loved Fiona, her BFF, who showed the reader how to be a true friend. Her bubbly spirit and "can-do" spirit was refreshing. I enjoyed learning from Jessica how to be open to new experiences and not to be afraid to befriend people who might be physically different or facing their own challenges. Jessica did not wallow in self-pity or blaming others. She put her mind and body into recovery. I highly recommend this read for any middle school student who feels overwhelmed at times. Runners and athletes will especially enjoy this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="681737428069337748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('E8ftJNVTqUdI23gz/B7lWTldlOTXQja6Yf2DlttSh02lewidqqRU7oOCK4Uwiko6m5JxivO9xyt8X7H7TonW2A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WDRPsWPvzSiYeR6ZozgDf4pkprUf+HnqnAXsOENoU1HuiKoIHBgwgVMgTS9vrKwcKKtD2zsHiHuBp95V1rMCxA==')})
  }

So when her little brother Jamie is shipped out of London to escape the war, Ada doesn’t waste a minute—she sneaks out to join him.   So begins a new adventure of Ada, and for Susan Smith, the woman who is forced to take the two kids in. As Ada teaches herself to ride a pony, learns to read, and watches for German spies, she begins to trust Susan—and Susan begins to love Ada and Jamie. But in the end, will their bond be enough to hold them together through wartime? Or will Ada and her brother fall back into the cruel hands of their mother?   This masterful work of historical fiction is equal parts adventure and a moving tale of family and identity—a classic in the making.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"8572898300254362957\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div class=\'wtrButtonContainer <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8571599224709115782">Wendelin Van Draanen has written more than thirty novels for young readers and teens. She is the author of the 18-book Edgar-winning Sammy Keyes series, and wrote Flipped which was named a Top 100 Children’s Novel for the 21st Century by SLJ, and became a Warner Brothers feature film with Rob Reiner directing. Her novel The Running Dream was awarded ALA’s Schneider Family Award for its portrayal o</span>
  <span id="freeText8571599224709115782" style="display:none">Wendelin Van Draanen has written more than thirty novels for young readers and teens. She is the author of the 18-book Edgar-winning Sammy Keyes series, and wrote Flipped which was named a Top 100 Children’s Novel for the 21st Century by SLJ, and became a Warner Brothers feature film with Rob Reiner directing. Her novel The Running Dream was awarded ALA’s Schneider Family Award for its portrayal of the disability experience.<br /><br />Van Draanen is also the author of two short chapter-book series. The Gecko &amp; Sticky books, are fun read-alouds, perfect for reluctant readers, and the Shredderman books—featuring a boy who deals with a bully—received the Christopher Award for “affirming the highest values of the human spirit” and became a Nickelodeon made-for-TV movie.<br /><br />Van Draanen was a classroom teacher for fifteen years. She and her husband reside in California and have two sons.<br /></span>
